intended to provide a minimal baseline set of requirements that are			intended to provide a minimal baseline set of requirements that are
targeted at mitigating well defined and described threats.				targeted at mitigating well defined and described threats.

product that in addition to the 802.11 [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) capability,			product that in addition to the 802.11 [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) capability,

### 1.3.1 TOE Boundary {#TOEboundary .indexable data-level="3"}				### 1.3.1 TOE Boundary {#TOEboundary .indexable data-level="3"}

This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) specifically addresses				This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) specifically addresses
[WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)/[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS). A conformant [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)			[WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)/[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS). A conformant [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)
is a product that can monitor, collect, inspect, and analyze real-time			is a product that can monitor, collect, inspect, and analyze real-time
network traffic and alert the administrator of policy violations.			network traffic and alert the administrator of policy violations.
[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS) functionality is not required to conform to this			[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS) functionality is not required to conform to this
[PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module), and it is optional for the				[PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module), and it is optional for the
[TOE](#abbr_TOE) to have the additional ability to react in real-time to		[TOE](#abbr_TOE) to have the additional ability to react in real-time to
potentially malicious wireless (IEEE 802.11) network traffic.				potentially malicious wireless (IEEE 802.11) network traffic.

Tests										      <
:::										      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Per guidance in [FMT\_SMF.1/WIDS](#FMT_SMF.1/WIDS),		      <
        add [MAC](#abbr_MAC) Addresses or other unique device identifier	      <
        for an [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the allowlist.		      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy the [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD) that		      <
        were added to allowlist within the range of the				      <
        [TOE](#abbr_TOE)\'s sensors.						      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the devices are classified as			      <
        authorized.								      <
    -   **Step 4:** Remove the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) from the allowlist.		      <
    -   **Step 5:** Verify that the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) is classified as		      <
        unauthorized.								      <
    -   **Step 6:** Remove the [AP](#abbr_AP) from the allowlist.		      <
    -   **Step 7:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) is classified as		      <
        unauthorized.								      <
-   **Test 2:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD), and connect the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the list of detected APs and EUDs		      <
        contains the allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD)		      <
        that were just deployed.						      <
    -   **Step 3:** If the [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD) are		      <
        detected verify that they are classified as allowlisted devices.	      <
-   **Test 3:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD) and connect the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the list of detected APs and EUDs		      <
        contains the non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD)	      <
        that were just deployed.						      <

a.  *Detection of the use of active [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) scanners (e.g.			a.  *Detection of the use of active [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) scanners (e.g.
    wardriving tools) to generate [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) traffic, such as			    wardriving tools) to generate [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) traffic, such as
    Probes, Auths, and Assoc frames*;						      |	    Probes, Auths, and Assoc frames*,
b.  *Detection of the physical location of an identified				b.  *Detection of the physical location of an identified
    [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) threat by using triangulation*;				      |	    [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) threat by using triangulation*,
c.  *Detection of an [SSID](#abbr_SSID) using						c.  *Detection of an [SSID](#abbr_SSID) using
    weak/unsupported/disallowed encryption options*;				      |	    weak/unsupported/disallowed encryption options*,
d.  *Detection of [AP](#abbr_AP) [SSID](#abbr_SSID) larger than 32			d.  *Detection of [AP](#abbr_AP) [SSID](#abbr_SSID) larger than 32
    bytes*;									      |	    bytes*,
e.  *Detection of excessive WPS negotiations*;					      |	e.  *\[**assignment**: [any other rules]{.assignable-content}\]*.
f.  *\[**assignment**: [any other rules]{.assignable-content}\]*\].		      <

::: {.appnote}										::: {.appnote}
[Application Note: ]{.note-header}[ These rules are used to detect a		      |	[Application Note: ]{.note-header}[ ]{.note}
potential security violation. Maintenance of the rules by adding,		      |
modifying or deletion of rules from the set of rules is handled by		      |	These rules are used to detect a potential security violation.
[FMT\_SMF.1/WIDS](#FMT_SMF.1/WIDS).]{.note}					      |	Maintenance of the rules by adding, modifying or deletion of rules from
										      >	the set of rules is handled by [FMT\_SMF.1/WIDS](#FMT_SMF.1/WIDS).

If a potential security violation is detected the alert generated for			If a potential security violation is detected the alert generated for
the Administrator is handled by [FAU\_ARP.1](#FAU_ARP.1).				the Administrator is handled by [FAU\_ARP.1](#FAU_ARP.1).
:::											:::
										      <
::: {.activity_pane .hide}							      <
::: {.activity_pane_header}							      <
[[ Evaluation Activity ]{.activity_pane_label}[]{.toggler}](#)			      <
:::										      <
										      <
::: {.activity_pane_body}							      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
[TSS](#abbr_TSS)								      <
:::										      <
										      <
The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS) describes the		      <
ability of the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to detect the network behavior described	      <
by the [SFR](#abbr_SFR). The evaluator shall verify that the			      <
[TSS](#abbr_TSS) describes the methods that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) uses to	      <
detect the presence of unauthorized connections and unauthorized network	      <
traffic. The evaluator shall examine the [TSS](#abbr_TSS) to verify that	      <
it describes the denial of service attacks that can be detected by the		      <
[TOE](#abbr_TOE). The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS)		      <
describes the ability of the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to detect when			      <
unauthorized [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) authentication schemes and encryption		      <
schemes are used. The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS)		      <
describes the ability of the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to detect when			      <
unauthorized APs and EUDs send or receive unencrypted data.			      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
Guidance									      <
:::										      <
										      <
If the ability of the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to detect the different potential	      <
security violations is configurable, the evaluator shall verify that the	      <
operational guidance provides instructions on how to configure the		      <
[TOE](#abbr_TOE).								      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
Tests										      <
:::										      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:** **Detection of non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP)**:		      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) is detected as a		      <
        non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 2:** **Detection of non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD)**:		      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) is detected as an		      <
        non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD).					      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 3:** **Detection of authorized [EUD](#abbr_EUD) establishing		      <
    peer-to-peer connection with any other [EUD](#abbr_EUD)**:			      <
    -   **Test 3.1:** Create the following connections between two		      <
        allowlisted EUDs.							      <
        -   Windows Ad Hoc Connection						      <
        -   Mac OS Ad Hoc							      <
        -   Linux Ad Hoc							      <
        -   Wi-Fi Direct							      <
    -   **Test 3.2:** Create the following connections between one		      <
        allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) and a non-allowlisted			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD)							      <
        -   Windows Ad Hoc Connection						      <
        -   Mac OS Ad Hoc							      <
        -   Linux Ad Hoc							      <
        -   Wi-Fi Direct							      <
										      <
    Verify that alerts were generated by each of the connections in each	      <
    test.									      <
-   **Test 4:** **Detection of [EUD](#abbr_EUD) bridging two network		      <
    interfaces**:\								      <
    Bridge two network interfaces on an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD)		      <
    (one must be the wireless card listed as allowlisted).			      <
    -   Create a Windows Hosted Network with an allowlisted			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD).							      <
    -   Connect a different allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the network.	      <
										      <
    Verify that alerts were generated by each of the connections in each	      <
    test.									      <
-   **Test 5:** **Detection of unauthorized point to point wireless		      <
    bridges by allowlisted APs**:						      <
    -   **Step 1:** Setup a point-to-point wireless bridge using		      <
        allowlisted APs in the range of the wireless sensors.			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verift that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the bridge.	      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 6:** **Alert generated by violation of user defined			      <
    signature**:								      <
    -   **Step 1:** Setup a user defined detection signature.			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) generates an alert		      <
        once the rules of signature have been violated.				      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 7:** **Detection of ICS connection**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Setup an Internet Connection Sharing (ICS)			      <
        connection.								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        establishment of the ICS connection.					      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 8:** **Detection of traffic with excessive transmit power		      <
    level**:									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure a source of network traffic that can		      <
        exceed the maximum transmit power levels of 100mW on 2.4GHz and		      <
        200mW on 5GHz.								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure a user defined signature to detects		      <
        traffic with transmit power levels that exceed the maximum.		      <
    -   **Step 3:** Commence with the transmission of network traffic at	      <
        excessive power levels.							      <
    -   **Step 4:** Collect wireless traffic with range of the			      <
        [TSF](#abbr_TSF).							      <
    -   **Step 5:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects wireless		      <
        traffic that exceeds 100mW on 2.4GHz and 200mW on 5GHz.			      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 9:** **Detection of [MAC](#abbr_MAC) spoofing**:			      <
    -   **Test 9.1:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Spoof mac address of allowliste [EUD](#abbr_EUD)	      <
            connected to an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) on a second		      <
            [EUD](#abbr_EUD).							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect [EUD](#abbr_EUD) with spoofed			      <
            [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address to another allowlisted			      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) while the valid [EUD](#abbr_EUD) it is		      <
            spoofing is connected to the first [AP](#abbr_AP).			      <
        -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detected the		      <
            [MAC](#abbr_MAC) spoofing.						      <
    -   **Test 9.2:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Spoof mac address of allowliste [AP](#abbr_AP)		      <
            on a second [AP](#abbr_AP).						      <
        -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detected the		      <
            [MAC](#abbr_MAC) spoofing.						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 10:** **Detection of unauthorized [AP](#abbr_AP) broadcasting	      <
    authorized SSIDs**:								      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) to		      <
        operate on a set channel on the 2.4 GHz band broadcasting an		      <
        authorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID).						      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) broadcasting an authorized		      <
        [SSID](#abbr_SSID).							      <
    -   **Step 3:** Repeat the test utilizing the 5 GHz band.			      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 11:** **Detection of authorized [AP](#abbr_AP) broadcasating		      <
    an unathorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID)**:					      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) to operate		      <
        on a set channel on the 2.4 GHz band broadcasting an			      <
        unauthorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID).					      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) broadcasting an authorized		      <
        [SSID](#abbr_SSID).							      <
    -   **Step 3:** Repeat the test utilizing the 5 GHz band.			      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 12:** **Detection of allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) connected		      <
    to unauthorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID)**:					      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) to operate		      <
        on a set channel on the 2.4 GHz band with an unauthorized		      <
        [SSID](#abbr_SSID).							      <
    -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) associated to the allowlisted		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP) broadcasting an unauthorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID).		      <
    -   **Step 4:** Repeat the test utilizing the 5 GHz band.			      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 13:** **Detection of NULL [SSID](#abbr_SSID) associations**:		      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure the [AP](#abbr_AP) to have null			      <
        [SSID](#abbr_SSID).							      <
    -   **Step 3:** Attempt to connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD)		      <
        to the [AP](#abbr_AP) without supplying the correct			      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP) [SSID](#abbr_SSID).					      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) does not permit the		      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to complete an association by returning a Probe	      <
        Request.								      <
    -   **Step 5:** If an association does occur, confirm that an alert		      <
        is triggered due to a violation of policy.				      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 14:** **Detection of active probing**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Perform an active scan on the subnet of the			      <
        [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN).							      <
    -   **Step 2:** Record tools used and type of scan performed.		      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the active		      <
        probing.								      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 15:** **Detection of packet flooding/[DoS](#abbr_DoS)/DDoS**:	      <
    -   **Step 1:** Generate a large amount of TCP and UDP traffic from		      <
        a single [EUD](#abbr_EUD).						      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        network-based [DoS](#abbr_DoS).						      <
    -   **Step 3:** Generate a large amount of TCP and UDP traffic from		      <
        multiple EUDs.								      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        network-based DDoS.							      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 16:** **Detection of RF-based denial of service**:			      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure		      <
        to stay in a particular channel.					      <
    -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 3:** Use an RF Jammer or signal generator on the same		      <
        frequency as the [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to create a	      <
        RF-based [DoS](#abbr_DoS).						      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) detects the		      <
        RF-based [DoS](#abbr_DoS).						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 17:** **Detection of deauthentication flooding**:			      <
    -   **Test 17.1:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure		      <
            to a set channel.							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 3:** Send an flood of deauthentication frames to the		      <
            [EUD](#abbr_EUD) using the [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address of		      <
            allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) it is connected to.			      <
        -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
            deauthentication flood.						      <
    -   **Test 17.2:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure		      <
            to a set channel.							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 3:** Send an flood of deauthentication frames with		      <
            the [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address of allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP)		      <
            as the source and destination as a broadcast.			      <
        -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
            deauthentication flood.						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 18:** **Detection of disassociation flooding**:			      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and connect		      <
        authorized EUDs.							      <
    -   **Step 2:** Generate disassociation frames from an unauthorized		      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD).							      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detected the		      <
        disassociation flooding.						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 19:** **Detection of request-to-send/clear-to-send abuse**:		      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure to a	      <
        set channel.								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Connect two allowlisted EUDs to the [AP](#abbr_AP).		      <
    -   **Step 3:** Send an flood of CTS frames to reserve RF medium.		      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the CTS		      <
        abuse.									      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 20:** **Detection of unauthorized authentication scheme		      <
    use**:\									      <
    The evaluator shall configure the [TOE](#abbr_TOE), per			      <
    [FMT\_SMF.1/WIDS](#FMT_SMF.1/WIDS), with 802.1x authentication as		      <
    the only mode of authorized [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) authentication		      <
    scheme.									      <
    -   **Test 20.1:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) with open		      <
            authentication.							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) using unauthorized		      <
            authentication schemes.						      <
    -   **Test 20.2:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) that uses		      <
            pre-shared key authentication.					      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) using unauthorized		      <
            authentication schemes.						      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 21:** **Detection of unauthorized encryption scheme use**:		      <
    -   **Test 21.1:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) with 128 bit		      <
            [AES](#abbr_AES) encryption type as the only allowed		      <
            encryption scheme.							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) with no		      <
            encryption.								      <
        -   **Step 3:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) detects the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) using unauthorized		      <
            encryption schemes.							      <
    -   **Test 21.2:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) with 128 bit		      <
            [AES](#abbr_AES) encryption type as the only allowed		      <
            encryption scheme.							      <
        -   **Step 2:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) that uses		      <
            [TKIP](#abbr_TKIP) encryption only.					      <
        -   **Step 3:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP).							      <
        -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) using unauthorized		      <
            encryption schemes.							      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 22:** **Detection of unencrypted traffic**:				      <
    -   **Test 22.1:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) with no		      <
            encryption.								      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and generate traffic.				      <
        -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) detects		      <
            unencrypted data frames being sent between the allowlisted		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD).				      <
        -   **Step 4:** Connect a non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and generate traffic.				      <
        -   **Step 5:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects		      <
            unencrypted data frames being sent between the allowlisted		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD).		      <
    -   **Test 22.2:**								      <
        -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) with no		      <
            encryption.								      <
        -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and generate traffic.				      <
        -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects		      <
            unencrypted data frames being between the non-allowlisted		      <
            [AP](#abbr_AP) and allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD).			      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 23:** **Detection of allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) or			      <
    [AP](#abbr_AP) that is using weak/outdated [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN)		      <
    protocols and protocol implementations**:					      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) that utilizes		      <
        the 802.11g or older [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) protocol.			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects the		      <
        weak/outdated [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) protocol and generates an		      <
        alert.									      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 24:** **Detection of extremely high numbers of client devices	      <
    using a particular allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP)**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure a threshold amount of client devices that		      <
        can use a particular [AP](#abbr_AP).					      <
    -   **Step 3:** Connect enough client devices to the [AP](#abbr_AP)		      <
        to purposely exceed the defined threshold.				      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when the		      <
        client usage exceeds the threshold.					      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 25:** **Detection of a high number of failed attempts to join	      <
    the [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) in a short period of time**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure a threshold amount of connection attempts		      <
        that can occur in a particular timeframe.				      <
    -   **Step 3:** Attempt to authenticate to the [AP](#abbr_AP) with		      <
        enough client devices to purposely exceed the defined threshold.	      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when the		      <
        connection attempts within the specic timeframe exceeds the		      <
        threshold.								      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 26:** **Detection of the use of active [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN)		      <
    scanners (e.g. wardriving tools) to generate [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN)		      <
    traffic**:									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when		      <
        [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) scanners are the source of [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN)	      <
        traffic.								      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 27:** **Detection of the physical location of an identified		      <
    [WLAN](#abbr_WLAN) threat by using triangulation**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) or			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD) within range of the [TSF](#abbr_TSF).			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) can track and		      <
        locate the [AP](#abbr_AP) or [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to within 5		      <
        meters.									      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 28:** **Detection of an [SSID](#abbr_SSID) using			      <
    weak/unsupported/disallowed encryption options**:				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure		      <
        its encryption options.							      <
    -   **Step 2:** Change the encryption options the [AP](#abbr_AP)		      <
        advertises.								      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP)\'s encryption options change.				      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 29:** **Detection of [AP](#abbr_AP) [SSID](#abbr_SSID) larger	      <
    than 32 bytes**:								      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and configure		      <
        its [SSID](#abbr_SSID) to be larger than 32 bytes.			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure a user defined signature on the			      <
        [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) to detect when an [SSID](#abbr_SSID) is		      <
        larger than 32 bytes.							      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP)\'s [SSID](#abbr_SSID) is larger than 32 bytes.		      <
										      <
    \										      <
-   **Test 30:** **Detection of excessive WPS negotiations**:			      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and permit WPS		      <
        authentication.								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Configure a threshold amount of WPS connections that	      <
        are allowed in a specific amount of time on the [AP](#abbr_AP)		      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detects when the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP)\'s WPS connection threshold has been exceeded.		      <
										      <
    \										      <

The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS) describes how the		      <

::: {.eacategory}								      <
Tests										      <
:::										      <
										      <
For test 1 and 2 below the evaluator shall verify that the			      <
[TOE](#abbr_TOE) detects and appropriately classifies the APs and EUDs.		      <
It is acceptable if the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) uses different but equivalent		      <
descriptors for the classification. If the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) does not		      <
support automatic detection metrics and equates a non-allowlisted		      <
[AP](#abbr_AP)/[EUD](#abbr_EUD) as malicious, than it is sufficient that	      <
the the classification given to the [AP](#abbr_AP)/[EUD](#abbr_EUD) in		      <
step 1 is the same as in step 2. If the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) supports		      <
automatic detection metrics and distinguishes between a non-allowlisted		      <
[AP](#abbr_AP)/[EUD](#abbr_EUD) and a malicious					      <
[AP](#abbr_AP)/[EUD](#abbr_EUD), then the classification for the		      <
[AP](#abbr_AP)/[EUD](#abbr_EUD) should differ between step 1 and step 2.	      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) in the area		      <
        of the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) sensor, but take no action against the	      <
        network. Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) is classified as		      <
        non-authorized.								      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) in the area		      <
        of the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) sensor and launch an attack against		      <
        the network. This can be any variation of Fake [AP](#abbr_AP),		      <
        Spoof [AP](#abbr_AP), Flood or [DoS](#abbr_DoS) attack.			      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) is classified as		      <
        malicious.								      <
-   **Test 2:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy a non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in the		      <
        area of the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) sensor, but take no action		      <
        against the network. Verify that the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) is		      <
        classified as non-authorized.						      <
    -   **Step 2:** Launch an RF Flooding, DoD/DDoS, masqueraded or		      <
        spoofing attack against authorized [AP](#abbr_AP) with an		      <
        unauthorized [EUD](#abbr_EUD).						      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) is classified as		      <
        malicious.								      <
-   **Test 3:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy an [AP](#abbr_AP) with an unauthorized		      <
        [SSID](#abbr_SSID) in the area of the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) sensor.	      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) detects the		      <
        unauthorized [SSID](#abbr_SSID).					      <

::: {.eacategory}								      <
[TSS](#abbr_TSS)								      <
:::										      <
										      <
The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS) includes which		      <
channels the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) can detect and monitor. Additionally, the		      <
[TSS](#abbr_TSS) shall include whether the [TOE](#abbr_TOE)			      <
simultaneously or nonsimultaneously monitors network traffic across		      <
these channels. The evaluator shall verify that the [TSS](#abbr_TSS)		      <
includes information on if the sensors are completely passive, by		      <
default, or if the sensors ability to transmit data is configurable.		      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
Guidance									      <
:::										      <
										      <
The evaluator shall review the operational guidance for how to configure	      <
the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) to monitor the channels as selected in the			      <
[SFR](#abbr_SFR). If the sensor ability to transmits data is			      <
configurable, the evaluator shall review the operational guidance for		      <
how to disable wireless transmissions from the sensor. The			      <
[TOE](#abbr_TOE) shall have the ability to perform stateful frame		      <
inspection and log attacks spanning multiple frames. The evaluator shall	      <
verify that the operational guidance provides instructions on how to		      <
specify and confirm that stateful frame capture and inspection is being		      <
performed.									      <
										      <
::: {.eacategory}								      <
Tests										      <
:::										      <
										      <
**Channels Monitored**								      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:** Channels on On 5GHz band					      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to monitor the		      <
        channels as selected in the [SFR](#abbr_SFR).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy an [AP](#abbr_AP) on at least 2 different		      <
        channels within the regulatory domain on 5GHz band.			      <
    -   **Step 3:** Deploy an [AP](#abbr_AP) on at least 2 different		      <
        channels outside the regulatory domain on 5GHz band.			      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) gets detected on each	      <
        channel tested.								      <
-   **Test 2:** Channels on 2.4GHz band						      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to monitor the		      <
        channels as selected in the [SFR](#abbr_SFR).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy [AP](#abbr_AP) on at least 2 different		      <
        channels within the regulatory domain on 2.4GHz band.			      <
    -   **Step 3:** Deploy [AP](#abbr_AP) on at least 2 different		      <
        channels outside the regulatory domain on 2.4GHz band.			      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) gets detected on each	      <
        channel tested.								      <
-   **Test 3:** Channels on 4.9GHz band (if selected)				      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to monitor the		      <
        channels specified in the [SFR](#abbr_SFR).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy [AP](#abbr_AP) and set to channels within the	      <
        4.9 GHz band outlined in the [TSS](#abbr_TSS).				      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) gets detected on each	      <
        channel tested.								      <
-   **Test 4:** Non-standard channel frequencies (if selected)			      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to monitor the		      <
        channels as selected in the [SFR](#abbr_SFR).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Deploy [AP](#abbr_AP) on at least 2 different		      <
        channels on non-standard channel frequencies.				      <
    -   **Step 3:** Verify that the [AP](#abbr_AP) gets detected on each	      <
        channel tested.								      <
										      <
**Wireless Sensor Transmission of Data**					      <
										      <
If the [TOE](#abbr_TOE) provides the ability to disable wireless		      <
transmission, the evaluator shall follow the operational guidance to		      <
configure the sensor to not transmit wirelessly.The evaluator shall		      <
then deploy a signal analyzer in order to check for wireless emanations		      <
from the [TOE](#abbr_TOE).\							      <
Repeat the two tests below, for both the 2.4GHz and the 5 GHz band.\		      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Boot a sensor and using the signal analyzer observe		      <
        to check if any eminations are coming from the sensor.			      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the signal analyzer does not pick up		      <
        emanations from the sensor.						      <
-   **Test 2:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** During normal sensor operations, observe the		      <
        analyzer for about 10 minutes to check if any eminations are		      <
        coming from the sensor.							      <
    -   **Step 2:** Verify that the signal analyzer does not pick up		      <
        emanations from the sensor.						      <
										      <
**Stateful Frame Inspection**							      <
										      <
-   **Test 1:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Deploy allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP).				      <
    -   **Step 2:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to the		      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 3:** Deploy a protocol analyzer or native capability		      <
        within the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) Controller between the			      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP) and [EUD](#abbr_EUD).					      <
    -   **Step 4:** Verify from the network traffic packet capture that		      <
        all frames are being inspected to validate their connection		      <
        state from the [TSF](#abbr_TSF)						      <
:::										      <
:::										      <

										      >	[FPT\_FLS.1](#FPT_FLS.1) supports the objective by ensuring that a
										      >	potential compromise of the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) triggers the
										      >	[TOE](#abbr_TOE) to fail into a secure state, which prevents
										      >	unauthorized administration.
										      >
										      >	[O.TRUSTED\_COMMUNICATIONS](#O.TRUSTED_COMMUNICATIONS)\
										      >
										      >	[FCO\_CPC\_EXT.1](#FCO_CPC_EXT.1) (from [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP))
										      >
										      >	[FCO\_CPC\_EXT.1](#FCO_CPC_EXT.1) supports the objective by ensuring
										      >	that distributed components are properly registered and authenticated.
										      >
										      >	[FPT\_ITT.1](#FPT_ITT.1) (from [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP))
										      >
										      >	[FPT\_ITT.1](#FPT_ITT.1) supports the objective by defining the trusted
										      >	communications protocol used to secure communications between
										      >	[TOE](#abbr_TOE) components.
										      >
										      >	[FTP\_ITC.1](#FTP_ITC.1) (from [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP))
										      >
										      >	[FTP\_ITC.1](#FTP_ITC.1) supports the objective by defining the trusted
										      >	communications protocol used to secure communications between the
										      >	[TOE](#abbr_TOE) and its operational environment.
										      >
										      >	5.4 TOE Security Assurance Requirements {#mod-sars .indexable data-level="2"}
										      >	---------------------------------------
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) does not define any [SARs](#abbr_SAR)
										      >	beyond those defined within the [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP) to which it can
										      >	claim conformance. It is important to note that a [TOE](#abbr_TOE) that
										      >	is evaluated against this [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) is inherently
										      >	evaluated against the NDcPP as well. This [PP](#abbr_PP) includes a
										      >	number of EAs associated with both Security Functional Requirements
										      >	([SFRs](#abbr_SFR)) and [SARs](#abbr_SAR). Additionally, this
										      >	[PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) includes a number of [SFR](#abbr_SFR)-based
										      >	EAs that similarly refine the [SARs](#abbr_SAR) of the
										      >	[Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP). The evaluation laboratory will evaluate the
										      >	[TOE](#abbr_TOE) against the chosen [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP) and
										      >	supplement that evaluation with the necessary [SFRs](#abbr_SFR) that are
										      >	taken from this [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module).
										      >

										      >
										      >	### 6.1.4 Consistency of Requirements {#conreq-b-nd .indexable data-level="3"}
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) identifies several [SFRs](#abbr_SFR)
										      >	from the NDcPP that are needed to support Wireless Intrusion
										      >	Detection/Prevention Systems ([WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)/[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS))
										      >	functionality. This is considered to be consistent because the
										      >	functionality provided by the NDcPP is being used for its intended
										      >	purpose. The [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) also identifies a number of
										      >	modified [SFRs](#abbr_SFR) from the NDcPP that are used entirely to
										      >	provide functionality for Wireless Intrusion Detection/Prevention
										      >	Systems ([WIDS](#abbr_WIDS)/[WIPS](#abbr_WIPS)). The rationale for why
										      >	this does not conflict with the claims defined by the NDcPP are as
										      >	follows:
										      >
										      >	[PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) Requirement
										      >
										      >	Consistency Rationale
										      >
										      >	Modified [SFRs](#abbr_SFR)
										      >
										      >	[FAU\_GEN\_EXT.1](#FAU_GEN_EXT.1)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) mandates the inclusion of this
										      >	selection-based [SFR](#abbr_SFR) because a [TOE](#abbr_TOE) that
										      >	conforms to this [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) will always be deployed in
										      >	a configuration that requires this [SFR](#abbr_SFR) to be claimed.
										      >
										      >	[FAU\_STG\_EXT.1](#FAU_STG_EXT.1)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) modifies the [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP)
										      >	[SFR](#abbr_SFR) to remove a selection that is not permitted by the
										      >	[TOE](#abbr_TOE) architecture that it specifies.
										      >
										      >	[FCO\_CPC\_EXT.1](#FCO_CPC_EXT.1)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) mandates the inclusion of this
										      >	optional [SFR](#abbr_SFR) because it is required to implement
										      >	functionality required by this [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module).
										      >
										      >	[FPT\_ITT.1](#FPT_ITT.1)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) mandates the inclusion of this
										      >	optional [SFR](#abbr_SFR) because it is required to implement
										      >	functionality required by this [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module).
										      >
										      >	[FTP\_ITC.1](#FTP_ITC.1)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) refines the [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP)
										      >	[SFR](#abbr_SFR) to add a selection for a specific external entity that
										      >	may be applicable to a [TOE](#abbr_TOE) that conforms to this
										      >	[PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module).
										      >
										      >	Additional [SFRs](#abbr_SFR)
										      >
										      >	This [PP-Module](#abbr_PP-Module) does not add any requirements when the
										      >	NDcPP is the base.

										      >	does not define an [SFR](#abbr_SFR) for this behavior but this
										      >	[SFR](#abbr_SFR) mitigates the T.SECURITY\_FUNCTIONALITY\_FAILURE threat
										      >	defined in the [Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP), so it is clear that this
										      >	behavior is consistent with the security expectations of the
										      >	[Base-PP](#abbr_Base-PP).

										      >

										      >	Implementation-based requirements.

        second [AP](#abbr_AP) in a shielded environment connected to the	      <
        valid network (Location 2).						      <
    -   **Step 4:** Spoof the [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address of the			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in location 1 with the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in		      <
        location 2 and connect it to the allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) in		      <
        location 2. Make sure both EUDs are connected at the same time.		      <
    -   **Step 5:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detected and		      <
        generated an alert.							      <
-   **Test 2:**									      <
    -   **Step 1:** Configure the timeframe allowed between connection		      <
        of two EUDs in two separate locations (Location 1, Location 2).		      <
    -   **Step 2:** Setup an allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) (Location 1).		      <
    -   **Step 3:** Connect an allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) to			      <
        [AP](#abbr_AP).								      <
    -   **Step 4:** Setup a second allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) and a		      <
        non-allowlisted [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in a separate non-overlapping		      <
        location where the [WIDS](#abbr_WIDS) also has sensors. Or		      <
        simulate the distant non-verlapping locations by deploying the		      <
        second [AP](#abbr_AP) in a shielded environment connected to the	      <
        valid network (Location 2).						      <
    -   **Step 5:** Spoof the [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address of the			      <
        [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in location 1 with the [EUD](#abbr_EUD) in		      <
        location 2 and connect it to the allowlisted [AP](#abbr_AP) in		      <
        location 2. Make sure that the time between connections is		      <
        shorter than the time timeframe allowed/configured.			      <
    -   **Step 6:** Verify that the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) detected and		      <
        generated an alert.							      <
:::											:::
										      >
										      >	#### Management: FAU\_INV\_EXT.5
										      >
										      >	No specific management functions are identified.
										      >
										      >	#### Audit: FAU\_INV\_EXT.5
										      >
										      >	There are no auditable events foreseen.

										      >	#### FAU\_MAC\_EXT.1 Device Impersonation
										      >
										      >	::: {style="margin-left: 1em;"}
										      >	Hierarchical to: No other components.
										      >
										      >	Dependencies to: [FAU\_INV\_EXT.2](#FAU_INV_EXT.2) Characteristics of
										      >	Environmental Objects
										      >
										      >	#### FAU\_MAC\_EXT.1.1 {#ext-comp-FAU_MAC_EXT.1.1}
										      >
										      >	The [TSF](#abbr_TSF) shall detect when two sensors in non-overlapping
										      >	locations receive traffic from the same [MAC](#abbr_MAC) address
										      >	simultaneously.
										      >
										      >	#### FAU\_MAC\_EXT.1.2 {#ext-comp-FAU_MAC_EXT.1.2}
										      >
										      >	The [TSF](#abbr_TSF) shall detect when two sensors in non-overlapping
										      >	locations receive traffic from the [MAC](#abbr_MAC) addresses of
										      >	non-allowlisted EUDs within an Authorized administrator-configurable
										      >	timeframe based on distance between sensors.
:::											:::
:::											:::
										      >
										      >	### C.2.1.9 FAU\_WIP\_EXT Wireless Intrusion Prevention {#ext-comp-FAU_WIP_EXT .index
										      >
										      >	::: {style="margin-left: 1em;"}
										      >	#### Family Behavior
										      >
										      >	<div>
										      >
										      >	This family defines requirements for wireless intrusion prevention.
										      >
										      >	</div>
										      >
										      >	#### Component Leveling
										      >
										      >	FAU\_WIP\_EXT1
										      >
										      >	[FAU\_WIP\_EXT.1](#FAU_WIP_EXT.1), Wireless Intrusion Prevention,
										      >	requires the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) to support reactive behavior if potential
										      >	malicious traffic is observed to be originating from or targeted to a
										      >	particular network asset.
										      >
										      >	#### Management: FAU\_WIP\_EXT.1
										      >
										      >	The following actions could be considered for the management functions
										      >	in FMT:
										      >
										      >	-   Enabling or disabling transmission of data by wireless sensor
										      >
										      >	#### Audit: FAU\_WIP\_EXT.1
										      >
										      >	The following actions should be auditable if FAU\_GEN Security Audit
										      >	Data Generation is included in the [PP](#abbr_PP)/[ST](#abbr_ST):
										      >
										      >	-   Isolation of [AP](#abbr_AP) or [EUD](#abbr_EUD)
										      >
										      >	#### FAU\_WIP\_EXT.1 Wireless Intrusion Prevention
										      >
										      >	::: {style="margin-left: 1em;"}
										      >	Hierarchical to: No other components.
										      >
										      >	Dependencies to: [FAU\_WID\_EXT.1](#FAU_WID_EXT.1) Wireless Intrusion
										      >	Detection - Malicious Environmental Objects
										      >
										      >	#### FAU\_WIP\_EXT.1.1 {#ext-comp-FAU_WIP_EXT.1.1}
										      >
										      >	The [TSF](#abbr_TSF) shall allow an Authorized Administrator to isolate
										      >	a wireless [AP](#abbr_AP) or [EUD](#abbr_EUD) from the network monitored
										      >	by the [TSF](#abbr_TSF) using the following methods: \[**selection**:
										      >	*wireless containment*, *wire-side containment of an unauthorized
										      >	[AP](#abbr_AP) connected to the internal corporate wired network*\].
										      >	:::
:::											:::
